lang="be">\xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x8c</span>, <i><i lang="be" title="Belarusian language text">Bie\xc5\x82aru\xc5\x9b</i></i>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Belarusian" title="Help:IPA/Belarusian">[b\xca\xb2\xc9\x9bla\xcb\x88rus\xca\xb2]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">\xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x8c</span>, <i><i lang="ru" title="Russian language text">Belarus\'</i></i>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Belarusian" title="Help:IPA/Belarusian">[b\xca\xb2\xc9\xaal\xc9\x90\xcb\x88rus\xca\xb2]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Belarus</b> (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">\xd0\xa0\xd1\x8d\xd1\x81\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd1\x96\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0 \xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x8c</span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>&#58; <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">\xd0\xa0\xd0\xb5\xd1\x81\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb8\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0 \xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x8c</span>), formerly known by its <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> name <b>Byelorussia</b> or <b>Belorussia</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>&#58; <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">\xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbe\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x81\xd0\xb8\xd1\x8f</span>, <i><i lang="ru" title="Russian language text">Byelorussiya</i></i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a><sup id="cite_ref-unee_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unee-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> bordered by <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> to the west, and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a> to the northwest. Its capital and most populous city is <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>. Over 40% of its 207,600 square kilometres (80,200&#160;sq&#160;mi) is forested. Its major economic sectors are service industries and manufacturing.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Until the 20th century, different states at various times controlled the lands of modern-day Belarus, including the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Polotsk" title="Principality of Polotsk">Principality of Polotsk</a> (11th to 14th centuries), the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.\n</p><p>In the aftermath of the 1917 <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>, Belarus declared independence as the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_People%27s_Republic" title="Belarusian People&#39;s Republic">Belarusian People\'s Republic</a>, which was conquered by Soviet Russia. The <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Soviet_Republic_of_Byelorussia" title="Socialist Soviet Republic of Byelorussia">Socialist Soviet Republic of Byelorussia</a> became a founding <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">constituent republic of the Soviet Union</a> in 1922 and was renamed as the <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (Byelorussian SSR). Belarus lost almost half of its territory to Poland after the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Soviet War">Polish\xe2\x80\x93Soviet War</a> of 1919\xe2\x80\x931921. Much of the borders of Belarus took their modern shape in 1939, when some lands of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Second Polish Republic</a> were reintegrated into it after the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland" title="Soviet invasion of Poland">Soviet invasion of Poland</a>, and were finalized after World War&#160;II.<sup id="cite_ref-uni1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uni2_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni2-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uni3_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> During WWII, military operations devastated Belarus, which lost about a third of its population and more than half of its economic resources.<sup id="cite_ref-axell_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-axell-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The republic was redeveloped in the post-war years. In 1945 the Byelorussian SSR became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, along with the Soviet Union and the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The parliament of the republic proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> of Belarus on <span class="nowrap">27 July</span> 1990, and during the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, Belarus declared independence on <span class="nowrap">25 August</span> 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lukashenko" title="Alexander Lukashenko">Alexander Lukashenko</a> has served as the country\'s first president since 1994. Belarus has been labeled "Europe\'s last dictatorship" by some Western journalists,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> on account of Lukashenko\'s self-described <a href="/wiki/Authoritarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> style of government.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRW_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Lukashenko continued a number of Soviet-era policies, such as <a href="/wiki/State_ownership" title="State ownership">state ownership</a> of large sections of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Belarus" title="Economy of Belarus">economy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Belarus" title="Elections in Belarus">Elections under Lukashenko\'s rule</a> have been widely criticized as unfair; and according to many countries and organizations, political opposition has been violently suppressed. Belarus is also the last country in Europe using the <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Belarus" title="Capital punishment in Belarus">death penalty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Belarus\'s <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> rating is the lowest in Europe, the country is labelled as "not free" by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>, as "repressed" in the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a>, and is rated as by far the worst country for <a href="/wiki/Press_freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Press freedom">press freedom</a> in Europe in the <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">2013\xe2\x80\x9314 Press Freedom Index</a> published by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, which ranks Belarus 157th out of 180 nations.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2000, Belarus and Russia signed a treaty for greater cooperation, forming the <a href="/wiki/Union_State" title="Union State">Union State</a>. Over 70% of Belarus\'s population of 9.49&#160;million resides in urban areas. More than 80% of the population is ethnic <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusian</a>, with sizable minorities of <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>. Since a referendum in 1995, the country has had two official languages: <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Belarus" title="Constitution of Belarus">Constitution of Belarus</a> does not declare any official religion, although the primary religion in the country is <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Orthodox_Church" title="Belarusian Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christianity</a>. The second-most widespread religion, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Belarus" title="Catholic Church in Belarus">Roman Catholicism</a>, has a much smaller following; nevertheless, Belarus celebrates both Orthodox and Catholic versions of Christmas and Easter as <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Belarus" title="Public holidays in Belarus">national holidays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Belarus is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since its founding, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organization" title="Collective Security Treaty Organization">CSTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Union" title="Eurasian Economic Union">EEU</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. Belarus has shown no aspirations for joining the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> but nevertheless maintains a <a href="/wiki/Belarus%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Belarus\xe2\x80\x93European Union relations">bilateral relationship with the organisation</a>, and likewise participates in two EU projects: the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Initiative" title="Baku Initiative">Baku Initiative</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctext">Military</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Administrative_divisions"><span class="tocnumber">4.6</span> <span class="toctext">Administrative divisions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Capital_punishment"><span class="tocnumber">4.7</span> <span class="toctext">Capital punishment</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Industry"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Industry</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Languages"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Languages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Arts_and_literature"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Arts and literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Dress"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Dress</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Telecommunications"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Telecommunications</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#World_Heritage_Sites"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">World Heritage Sites</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>\n<p>The name <i>Belarus</i> is closely related with the term <i>Belaya Rus<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span></i>, i.e., <i><a href="/wiki/White_Rus%27" class="mw-redirect" title="White Rus&#39;">White Rus\'</a></i>. There are several claims to the origin of the name <i>White Rus\'.</i><sup id="cite_ref-Zaprudnik_1993_2_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaprudnik_1993_2-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> An ethno-religious theory suggests that the name used to describe the part of old <a href="/wiki/Ruthenia" title="Ruthenia">Ruthenian</a> lands within the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a> that had been populated mostly by early Christianized <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Black_Ruthenia" title="Black Ruthenia">Black Ruthenia</a>, which was predominantly inhabited by pagan <a href="/wiki/Balts" title="Balts">Balts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An alternate explanation for the name comments on the white clothing worn by the local Slavic population.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaprudnik_1993_2_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaprudnik_1993_2-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> A third theory suggests that the old Rus\' lands that were not conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a> (i.e., Polotsk, Vitebsk and Mogilev) had been referred to as "White Rus\'".<sup id="cite_ref-Zaprudnik_1993_2_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaprudnik_1993_2-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The name <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rus&#39; (region)">Rus\'</a> is often conflated with its Latin forms <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruthenia" title="Ruthenia">Ruthenia</a>, thus Belarus is often referred to as <i>White Russia</i> or <i>White Ruthenia</i>. The name first appeared in <a href="/wiki/Medieval_German_literature" title="Medieval German literature">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Latin_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval Latin literature">Latin</a> <a href="/wiki/Medieval_literature" title="Medieval literature">medieval literature</a>; the chronicles of <a href="/wiki/Jan_of_Czarnk%C3%B3w" title="Jan of Czarnk\xc3\xb3w">Jan of Czarnk\xc3\xb3w</a> mention the imprisonment of Lithuanian grand duke <a href="/wiki/Jogaila" class="mw-redirect" title="Jogaila">Jogaila</a> and his mother at "<i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Albae Russiae, Poloczk dicto</i>" in 1381.<sup id="cite_ref-vauchez_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vauchez-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In some languages, including German, Afrikaans and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, the country is generally called "White Russia" to this day (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Wei\xc3\x9frussland</i></i> and <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Wit-Rusland</i></i> respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Latin term "Alba Russia" was used again by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_VI" title="Pope Pius VI">Pope Pius VI</a> in 1783 to recognize the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a> there, exclaiming "<i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Approbo Societatem Jesu in Alba Russia degentem, approbo, approbo</i>."<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The first known use of <i>White Russia</i> to refer to Belarus was in the late-16th century by Englishman Sir <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Horsey" title="Jerome Horsey">Jerome Horsey</a>, who was known for his close contacts with the Russian Royal Court.<sup id="cite_ref-alies_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alies-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> During the 17th century, the Russian <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">tsars</a> used "White Rus" to describe the lands added from the Grand Duchy of Lithuania.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stemp_Efrasinia_Polackaja.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Stemp_Efrasinia_Polackaja.jpg/180px-Stemp_Efrasinia_Polackaja.jpg" width="180" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Stemp_Efrasinia_Polackaja.jpg/270px-Stemp_Efrasinia_Polackaja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Stemp_Efrasinia_Polackaja.jpg/360px-Stemp_Efrasinia_Polackaja.jpg 2x" data-file-width="456" data-file-height="629" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stemp_Efrasinia_Polackaja.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stamp with the <a href="/wiki/Cross_of_Saint_Euphrosyne" title="Cross of Saint Euphrosyne">Cross of St. Euphrosyne</a> from 1992</div></div></div>\n<p>The term <i>Belorussia</i> (Russian: <span lang="ru">\xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbe\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xcc\x81\xd1\x81\xd1\x81\xd0\xb8\xd1\x8f</span>, the latter part similar but spelled and stressed differently from \xd0\xa0\xd0\xbe\xd1\x81\xd1\x81\xd0\xb8\xcc\x81\xd1\x8f, <i>Russia</i>) first rose in the days of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, and the Russian Tsar was usually styled "the Tsar of All the Russias", as <i>Russia</i> or the <i>Russian Empire</i> was formed by three parts of Russia\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Great_Russia" title="Great Russia">Great</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Russia" title="Little Russia">Little</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White_Ruthenia" title="White Ruthenia">White</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> This asserted that the territories are all Russian and all the peoples are also Russian; in the case of the Belarusians, they were variants of the Russian people.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik Revolution">Bolshevik Revolution</a> in 1917, the term "White Russia" caused some confusion, as it was also the name of the military force that opposed the red Bolsheviks.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> During the period of the Byelorussian SSR, the term <i>Byelorussia</i> was embraced as part of a national consciousness. In western Belarus under Polish control, <i>Byelorussia</i> became commonly used in the regions of <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82ystok" title="Bia\xc5\x82ystok">Bia\xc5\x82ystok</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grodno" title="Grodno">Grodno</a> during the interwar period.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The term <i>Byelorussia</i> (its names in other languages such as English being based on the Russian form) was only used officially until 1991, when the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_Belarus" title="Supreme Soviet of Belarus">Supreme Soviet</a> of the Byelorussian SSR decreed by law that the new independent republic should be called <i>Republic of Belarus</i> (<span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">\xd0\xa0\xd0\xb5\xd1\x81\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb8\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0 \xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x8c</span> spelled in Russian), as well its abridged form should be "Belarus". The law decreed that all the forms of the new term should be transliterated into other languages from their <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian language</a> forms. The use of Byelorussian SSR and any abbreviations thereof were allowed from 1991 to 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-bynamelaw_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bynamelaw-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Conservative forces in the newly independent Belarus did not support the name change and opposed its inclusion in the 1991 draft of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Belarus" title="Constitution of Belarus">Constitution of Belarus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Accordingly, the name <i>Byelorussia</i> was replaced by <i>Belarus</i> in English.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaprudnik_1993_4-5_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaprudnik_1993_4-5-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Likewise, the adjective <i>Belorussian</i> or <i>Byelorussian</i> was replaced by <i>Belarusian</i> in English. <i>Belarusian</i> is closer to the original Belarusian term of <i><i lang="be-Latn" title="Belarusian language text">bielaruski</i></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaprudnik_1993_4-5_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaprudnik_1993_4-5-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Belarusian intelligentsia in the <a href="/wiki/Stalin_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Stalin era">Stalin era</a> attempted to change the name from <i>Byelorussia</i> to a form of <i>Krivia</i> because of the supposed connection with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Some nationalists object to the name for the same reason.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-levy_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-levy-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Several local newspapers kept the old name of the country in Russian in their names, for example <i><i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian language text"><a href="/wiki/Komsomolskaya_Pravda" title="Komsomolskaya Pravda">Komsomolskaya Pravda v Byelorussii</a></i></i>, which is the localized publication of a popular Russian newspaper. Also, those who wish for Belarus to be reunited with Russia continue to use <i>Belorussia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-levy_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-levy-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Officially, the full name of the country is "Republic of Belarus" (<span lang="be" title="Belarusian language text">\xd0\xa0\xd1\x8d\xd1\x81\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd1\x96\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0 \xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x8c</span>, <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">\xd0\xa0\xd0\xb5\xd1\x81\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb8\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0 \xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x8c</span>, <i lang="be-Latn" title="Belarusian language text">Respublika Belarus</i> <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Be-Republic_of_Belarus.oga" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1b/Be-Republic_of_Belarus.oga" class="internal" title="Be-Republic of Belarus.oga">listen</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>\xc2\xb7<a href="/wiki/File:Be-Republic_of_Belarus.oga" title="File:Be-Republic of Belarus.oga"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-bynamelaw_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bynamelaw-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Belarus" title="History of Belarus">History of Belarus</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>\n<p>From 5000 to 2000 BC, <a href="/wiki/Bandkeramik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bandkeramik">Bandkeramik</a> cultures predominated. In addition, remains from the <a href="/wiki/Dnieper-Donets_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnieper-Donets culture">Dnieper-Donets culture</a> were found in Belarus and parts of <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">Cimmerians</a> and other pastoralists roamed through the area by 1,000 BC, and by 500 AD, Slavs had taken up residence, which was circumscribed by the <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> who roamed its outskirts. Invaders from Asia, among whom were the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avars</a>, swept through c. 400\xe2\x80\x93600 AD, but were unable to dislodge the Slavic presence.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The region that is now Belarus was first settled by <a href="/wiki/Baltic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltic peoples">Baltic</a> tribes in the 3rd century. Around the 5th century, the area was taken over by Slavic tribes. The takeover was partially due to the lack of military coordination of the Balts but the gradual assimilation of the Balts into Slavic culture was peaceful in nature.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_K_Polotsk_general.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alex_K_Polotsk_general.png/220px-Alex_K_Polotsk_general.png" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alex_K_Polotsk_general.png/330px-Alex_K_Polotsk_general.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alex_K_Polotsk_general.png/440px-Alex_K_Polotsk_general.png 2x" data-file-width="614" data-file-height="483" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_K_Polotsk_general.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Polotsk" title="Principality of Polotsk">Principality of Polotsk</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Principality_of_Polotsk">Principality of Polotsk</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus&#39;">Kievan Rus\'</a>, <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Polotsk" title="Principality of Polotsk">Principality of Polotsk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a></div>\n<p>In the 9th century some principalities arose on the territory of modern Belarus. Among them was the Principality of Polotsk that for most of the time was effectively an independent State (apart from about 20 years when it was a Vassal of Kievan Rus\'). The Principality of Polotsk was the first nation state to be established on the land of Belarus.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</span></h3>\n<p>Many early Rus\' principalities were virtually razed or severely affected by a major <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Rus&#39;">Mongol invasion</a> in the 13th century, but the lands of modern Belarus avoided the brunt of the invasion and were eventually joined the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are no sources of military seizure, but the annals affirm the alliance and united foreign policy of Polotsk and Lithuania for decades. For example, the Chronicle of Novgorod informs about "Izyaslav had been set to be Knyaz in Luki and covered Novgorod from the Lithuanians" in 1198 when Luki is situated on the east from Polotsk.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GDL_Map,_15cent.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/GDL_Map%2C_15cent.png/220px-GDL_Map%2C_15cent.png" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/GDL_Map%2C_15cent.png/330px-GDL_Map%2C_15cent.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/GDL_Map%2C_15cent.png/440px-GDL_Map%2C_15cent.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1529" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GDL_Map,_15cent.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a> in the 15th century. Belarus was fully within its borders.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Grand Duchy of Lithuania, whose territory started its existence between Nemunas and Neris rivers and existed in the center of Europe in the 13th\xe2\x80\x9318th centuries and comprised entire territories of contemporary Belarus, Ukraine, partially Poland, Lithuania and Latvia and stretched from the Baltic Sea to the Black Sea.\n</p><p>Incorporation into the Grand Duchy of Lithuania resulted in an economic, political and ethno-cultural unification of Belarusian lands.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Of the principalities held by the Duchy, nine of them were settled by a population that would eventually become Belarusian people.<sup id="cite_ref-zaprudnik_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zaprudnik-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> During this time, the Duchy was involved in several military campaigns, including fighting on the side of Poland against the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Teutonic Knights">Teutonic Knights</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grunwald" title="Battle of Grunwald">Battle of Grunwald</a> in 1410; the joint victory allowed the Duchy to control the northwestern borderlands of Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Muscovites</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Ivan_III_of_Russia" title="Ivan III of Russia">Ivan III of Moscow</a>, began military campaigns in 1486 in an attempt to incorporate the lands of Kievan Rus\', specifically the territories of modern Belarus, Russia and Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Polish.E2.80.93Lithuanian_Commonwealth"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian_Commonwealth">Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth</a></div>\n<p>On 2 February 1386, the Grand Duchy of Lithuania and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1025%E2%80%931385)" title="Kingdom of Poland (1025\xe2\x80\x931385)">Kingdom of Poland</a> were joined in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> through a <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Krewo" title="Union of Krewo">marriage of their rulers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> This union set in motion the developments that eventually resulted in the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>, created in 1569 by the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Lublin" title="Union of Lublin">Union of Lublin</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Magnus_ducatus_Lithuania,_1780.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Magnus_ducatus_Lithuania%2C_1780.jpg/220px-Magnus_ducatus_Lithuania%2C_1780.jpg" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Magnus_ducatus_Lithuania%2C_1780.jpg/330px-Magnus_ducatus_Lithuania%2C_1780.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Magnus_ducatus_Lithuania%2C_1780.jpg/440px-Magnus_ducatus_Lithuania%2C_1780.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2725" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Magnus_ducatus_Lithuania,_1780.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Modern Belarusian lands on a Tobias Lotter map of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>, 1780. Area occupied after the <a href="/wiki/First_Partition_of_Poland" title="First Partition of Poland">First Partition of Poland</a> marked in green.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Lithuanian nobles was forced to go for rapprochement because of the threat coming from <a href="/wiki/Muscovy" class="mw-redirect" title="Muscovy">Muscovy</a>.\nTo strengthen the independence in the format of the union, three editions of the <a href="/wiki/Statutes_of_Lithuania" title="Statutes of Lithuania">Statutes of Lithuania</a> were issued in the 16th century. \nThe third Article of the Statute establishes that all lands of Grand Duchy of Lithuania will be eternally in Grand Duchy of Lithuania and never enter as a part of other states. It allowed to own the land within Grand Duchy of Lithuania only to own families. Anyone from outside Duchy would be honored with property only own it after swearing to Grand Duke of Lithuania. These articles were aimed to defend the rights of the Grand Duchy of Lithuania nobility against Polish, Prussian and other aristocracy of <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>.\n</p><p>In the years following the union, the process of gradual <a href="/wiki/Polonization" title="Polonization">Polonization</a> of both Lithuanians and Ruthenians gained steady momentum. In culture and social life, both the Polish language and Catholicism became dominant, and in 1696, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> replaced Ruthenian as the official language\xe2\x80\x94with the Ruthenian language being banned from administrative use.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> However, the Ruthenian peasants, continued to speak their own language and remained faithful to the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Belarusian Greek Catholic Church">Belarusian Greek Catholic Church</a>. Statutes were initially only issued in <a href="/wiki/Ruthenian_language" title="Ruthenian language">Ruthenian language</a> and later also in Polish. Around 1840 the Statutes were banned by the Russian tsar following the <a href="/wiki/November_Uprising" title="November Uprising">November Uprising</a>. Modern Ukrainian lands used it until 1860s.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Empire">Russian Empire</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_Uprising" title="Ko\xc5\x9bciuszko Uprising">Ko\xc5\x9bciuszko Uprising</a>, <a href="/wiki/November_Uprising" title="November Uprising">November Uprising</a>, <a href="/wiki/January_Uprising" title="January Uprising">January Uprising</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_history_in_the_Russian_Empire" title="Belarusian history in the Russian Empire">Belarusian history in the Russian Empire</a></div>\n<p>The union between Poland and Lithuania ended in 1795 with the <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">partitioning of Poland</a> by Imperial Russia, <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Austria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The Belarusian territories acquired by the Russian Empire under the reign of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_II_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Catherine II of Russia">Catherine&#160;II</a><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> were included into the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Governorate" title="Belarusian Governorate">Belarusian Governorate</a> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>&#58; <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">\xd0\x91\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbe\xd1\x80\xd1\x83\xd1\x81\xd1\x81\xd0\xba\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb5 \xd0\xb3\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb5\xd1\x80\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbb-\xd0\xb3\xd1\x83\xd0\xb1\xd0\xb5\xd1\x80\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0\xd1\x82\xd0\xbe\xd1\x80\xd1\x81\xd1\x82\xd0\xb2\xd0\xbe</span>) in 1796 and held until their occupation by the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-olson95_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olson95-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kosciol_Sw_Szymona_i_Sw_Heleny_Minsk_-_2013_AD_f.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Kosciol_Sw_Szymona_i_Sw_Heleny_Minsk_-_2013_AD_f.JPG/220px-Kosciol_Sw_Szymona_i_Sw_Heleny_Minsk_-_2013_AD_f.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Kosciol_Sw_Szymona_i_Sw_Heleny_Minsk_-_2013_AD_f.JPG/330px-Kosciol_Sw_Szymona_i_Sw_Heleny_Minsk_-_2013_AD_f.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Kosciol_Sw_Szymona_i_Sw_Heleny_Minsk_-_2013_AD_f.JPG/440px-Kosciol_Sw_Szymona_i_Sw_Heleny_Minsk_-_2013_AD_f.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kosciol_Sw_Szymona_i_Sw_Heleny_Minsk_-_2013_AD_f.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saints_Simon_and_Helena" title="Church of Saints Simon and Helena">Church of Saints Simon and Helena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, then part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, 1910</div></div></div>\n<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia" title="Nicholas I of Russia">Nicholas I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Russia" title="Alexander III of Russia">Alexander III</a> the national cultures were repressed. Policies of <a href="/wiki/Polonization" title="Polonization">Polonization</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> changed by <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-zytko-1_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zytko-1-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> which included the return to <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christianity</a> of Belorusian <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Brest" title="Union of Brest">Uniates</a>. Belarusian language was banned in schools while in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Samogitia" title="Samogitia">Samogitia</a> primary school education with <a href="/wiki/Samogitian_dialect" title="Samogitian dialect">Samogitian</a> literacy was allowed.<sup id="cite_ref-\xd0\x9a\xd0\xbe\xd1\x80\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb21908_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-\xd0\x9a\xd0\xbe\xd1\x80\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb21908-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a> drive in the 1840s, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia" title="Nicholas I of Russia">Nicholas I</a> prohibited use of the Belarusian language in public schools, campaigned against Belarusian publications and tried to pressure those who had converted to Catholicism under the Poles to reconvert to the Orthodox faith. In 1863, economic and cultural pressure exploded in a <a href="/wiki/January_Uprising" title="January Uprising">revolt</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Konstanty_Kalinowski" title="Konstanty Kalinowski">Konstanty Kalinowski</a>. After the failed revolt, the Russian government reintroduced the use of <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic</a> to Belarusian in 1864 and no documents in Belarusian were permitted by the Russian government until 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the negotiations of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk_(Russia%E2%80%93Central_Powers)" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk (Russia\xe2\x80\x93Central Powers)">Treaty of Brest-Litovsk</a>, Belarus first declared independence under German occupation on <span class="nowrap">25 March</span> 1918, forming the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_People%27s_Republic" title="Belarusian People&#39;s Republic">Belarusian People\'s Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-birgerson_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-birgerson-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Immediately afterwards, the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Soviet War">Polish\xe2\x80\x93Soviet War</a> ignited, and the territory of Belarus was divided between Poland and Soviet Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\nThe Rada of the Belarusian Democratic Republic exists as a <a href="/wiki/Government_in_exile" title="Government in exile">government in exile</a> ever since then; in fact, it is currently the world\'s longest serving government in exile.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Belarusian_People.27s_Republic"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Belarusian_People\'s_Republic">Belarusian People\'s Republic</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_People%27s_Republic" title="Belarusian People&#39;s Republic">Belarusian People\'s Republic</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Postcard_BNR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Postcard_BNR.jpg/200px-Postcard_BNR.jpg" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Postcard_BNR.jpg/300px-Postcard_BNR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Postcard_BNR.jpg/400px-Postcard_BNR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2227" data-file-height="3339" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Postcard_BNR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Belarusian People\'s Republic postcard with Coats of Arms of voivodeships</div></div></div>\n<p>The Belarusian People\'s Republic was a first attempt to create an independent Belarusian state under name "Belarus". Despite the many efforts state ceased to exist cause territory was occupied and controlled by <a href="/wiki/German_Imperial_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="German Imperial Army">German Imperial Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Army" title="Imperial Russian Army">Imperial Russian Army</a> and than <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> times. It existed only from 1918 to 1919 but created prerequisites for the formation of the state idea around the newly name "Belarus" on these lands. The choice of the name was probably based the fact that the intelligent core of young government was educated in the tsardom universities with a corresponding education around the ideology of West-Russianism.<sup id="cite_ref-Jr.Zaprudnik2010_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jr.Zaprudnik2010-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Central_Lithuania">Republic of Central Lithuania</span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Central_Lithuania" title="Republic of Central Lithuania">Republic of Central Lithuania</a> was a short-lived political entity, which was the last attempt to restore Lithuania in the historical confederacy state (it was also supposed to create Lithuania Upper and Lithuania Lower). The republic was created in 1920 following <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBeligowski%27s_Mutiny" title="\xc5\xbbeligowski&#39;s Mutiny">the staged rebellion</a> of soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/1st_Lithuanian%E2%80%93Belarusian_Division" title="1st Lithuanian\xe2\x80\x93Belarusian Division">1st Lithuanian\xe2\x80\x93Belarusian Division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Army">Polish Army</a> under <a href="/wiki/Lucjan_%C5%BBeligowski" title="Lucjan \xc5\xbbeligowski">Lucjan \xc5\xbbeligowski</a>. Centered on the historical capital of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vilna" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilna">Vilna</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>: <i lang="lt">Vilnius</i>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">Wilno</i>), for 18 months the entity served as a <a href="/wiki/Buffer_state" title="Buffer state">buffer state</a> between <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, upon which it depended, and Lithuania, which claimed the area.<sup id="cite_ref-von_Rauch_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-von_Rauch-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> After a variety of delays, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Central_Lithuania_general_election,_1922" title="Republic of Central Lithuania general election, 1922">a disputed election</a> took place on 8 January 1922, and the territory was annexed to Poland. \xc5\xbbeligowski later in his memoir which was published in London in 1943 condemned the annexation of Republic by Poland, as well as the policy of closing Belarusian schools and general disregard of Marshal <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski" title="J\xc3\xb3zef Pi\xc5\x82sudski">J\xc3\xb3zef Pi\xc5\x82sudski</a>\'s confederation plans by Polish ally.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Years earlier interrogation report of 19-year-old revolutionary <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski" title="J\xc3\xb3zef Pi\xc5\x82sudski">Pilsudski</a> of March 10, 1887 indicated that he called himself a "belarusian, nobleman".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic">Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caricature_for_Riga_Peace_1921.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caricature_for_Riga_Peace_1921.png/275px-Caricature_for_Riga_Peace_1921.png" width="275" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caricature_for_Riga_Peace_1921.png/413px-Caricature_for_Riga_Peace_1921.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caricature_for_Riga_Peace_1921.png/550px-Caricature_for_Riga_Peace_1921.png 2x" data-file-width="1903" data-file-height="1311" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caricature_for_Riga_Peace_1921.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caricature illustrating the partition of Belarus between <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolsheviks</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Riga" title="Peace of Riga">Peace of Riga</a>, 1921</div></div></div>\n<p>A part of Belarus under Russian rule emerged as the <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (Byelorussian SSR) in 1919. Soon thereafter it merged to form the <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian%E2%80%93Belorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithuanian\xe2\x80\x93Belorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Lithuanian-Byelorussian SSR</a>. The contested lands were divided between Poland and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> after the war ended in 1921, and the Byelorussian SSR became a founding member of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics in 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-birgerson_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-birgerson-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The western part of modern Belarus remained part of Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-ocu1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocu1-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ocu2_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocu2-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1920s and 1930s, Soviet agricultural and economic policies, including <a href="/wiki/Collectivization" class="mw-redirect" title="Collectivization">collectivization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Five-Year_Plans_for_the_National_Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Five-Year Plans for the National Economy of the Soviet Union">five-year plans for the national economy</a>, led to famine and political repression.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Khatyn_Memorial,_Belarus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Khatyn_Memorial%2C_Belarus.jpg/220px-Khatyn_Memorial%2C_Belarus.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Khatyn_Memorial%2C_Belarus.jpg/330px-Khatyn_Memorial%2C_Belarus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Khatyn_Memorial%2C_Belarus.jpg/440px-Khatyn_Memorial%2C_Belarus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3750" data-file-height="2500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Khatyn_Memorial,_Belarus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Khatyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Khatyn">Khatyn</a> Memorial. During World War II, the Germans murdered civilians in 5,295 different localities in <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Belarus_by_Nazi_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of Belarus by Nazi Germany">occupied Soviet Belarus</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soviet_guerilla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Soviet_guerilla.jpg/220px-Soviet_guerilla.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Soviet_guerilla.jpg/330px-Soviet_guerilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Soviet_guerilla.jpg/440px-Soviet_guerilla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="770" data-file-height="508" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soviet_guerilla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Soviet_partisans#Belarus" title="Soviet partisans">Soviet partisan</a> fighters behind <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Front_line" title="Front line">front lines</a> in Belarus in 1943</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1939, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and the Soviet Union invaded and occupied Poland, marking the beginning of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The Soviets invaded and annexed much of eastern Poland, which had been part of the country since the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Riga" title="Peace of Riga">Peace of Riga</a> two decades earlier. Much of the northern section of this area was added to the Byelorussian SSR, and now constitutes <a href="/wiki/West_Belarus" class="mw-redirect" title="West Belarus">West Belarus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uni1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uni2_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni2-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uni3_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uni4_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni4-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The Soviet-controlled Byelorussian People\'s Council officially took control of the territories, whose populations consisted of a mixture of Poles, Ukrainians, Belarusians and Jews, on 28 October 1939 in <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82ystok" title="Bia\xc5\x82ystok">Bia\xc5\x82ystok</a>. Nazi Germany <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">invaded the Soviet Union</a> in 1941. The <a href="/wiki/Brest_Fortress" title="Brest Fortress">Brest Fortress</a>, which had been annexed in 1939, at this time was subjected to one of the most destructive onslaughts that happened during the war. Statistically, the Byelorussian SSR was the hardest-hit Soviet republic in World War II; it <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Belarus_by_Nazi_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of Belarus by Nazi Germany">remained in Nazi hands</a> until 1944. During that time, Germany destroyed 209 out of 290 cities in the republic, 85% of the republic\'s industry, and more than one million buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-axell_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-axell-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The Nazi <i><a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Generalplan Ost</a></i> called for the extermination, expulsion or enslavement of most or all Belarusians for the purpose of providing more <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">living space</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Drang_nach_Osten" title="Drang nach Osten">East</a> for Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="World War II casualties of the Soviet Union">Casualties</a> were estimated to be between 2 and 3 million (about a quarter to one-third of the total population), while the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Belarus" title="History of the Jews in Belarus">Jewish population of Belarus</a> was devastated during <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a> and never recovered.<sup id="cite_ref-axell_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-axell-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-warpop_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warpop-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The population of Belarus did not regain its pre-war level until 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-warpop_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warpop-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> It was also after this conflict that the final borders of Belarus were set by Stalin when parts of Belarusian territory were given to the recently annexed Lithuania.<sup id="cite_ref-uni4_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni4-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the war, Belarus was among the 51 founding countries of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" title="United Nations Charter">United Nations Charter</a> and as such it was allowed an additional vote at the UN, on top of the Soviet Union\'s vote. Vigorous postwar reconstruction promptly followed the end of the war and the Byelorussian SSR became a major center of manufacturing in the western USSR, creating jobs and attracting ethnic Russians.<sup id="cite_ref-Soviet-era_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soviet-era-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The borders of the Byelorussian SSR and Poland were redrawn, in accord with the 1919-proposed <a href="/wiki/Curzon_Line" title="Curzon Line">Curzon Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-olson95_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olson95-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> implemented a policy of <a href="/wiki/Sovietization" title="Sovietization">Sovietization</a> to isolate the Byelorussian SSR from <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western influences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-warpop_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warpop-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> This policy involved sending Russians from various parts of the Soviet Union and placing them in key positions in the Byelorussian SSR government. After Stalin\'s death in 1953, <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> continued his predecessor\'s <a href="/wiki/Cultural_hegemony" title="Cultural hegemony">cultural hegemony</a> program, stating, "The sooner we all start speaking Russian, the faster we shall build communism."<sup id="cite_ref-warpop_78-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warpop-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1986, the Byelorussian SSR was exposed to significant <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fallout" title="Nuclear fallout">nuclear fallout</a> from the explosion at the <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">Chernobyl</a> power plant in the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian SSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gorby_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gorby-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 1988, the archaeologist and leader of the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Christian_Party_%E2%80%93_BPF" title="Conservative Christian Party \xe2\x80\x93 BPF">Christian Conservative Party of the BPF</a> <a href="/wiki/Zyanon_Paznyak" class="mw-redirect" title="Zyanon Paznyak">Zyanon Paznyak</a> discovered <a href="/wiki/Mass_grave" title="Mass grave">mass graves</a> of victims executed in 1937\xe2\x80\x9341 at <a href="/wiki/Kurapaty" title="Kurapaty">Kurapaty</a>, near Minsk.<sup id="cite_ref-Gorby_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gorby-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Some nationalists contend that this discovery is proof that the Soviet government was trying to erase the Belarusian people, causing Belarusian nationalists to seek independence.<sup id="cite_ref-massgraves_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massgraves-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1438" data-file-height="945" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leaders of Russia, Ukraine and Belarus signed the <a href="/wiki/Belavezha_Accords" title="Belavezha Accords">Belavezha Accords</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolving the Soviet Union</a>, 8 December 1991</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h3>\n<p>In March 1990, elections for seats in the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet" title="Supreme Soviet">Supreme Soviet</a> of the Byelorussian SSR took place. Though the pro-independence <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Popular_Front" title="Belarusian Popular Front">Belarusian Popular Front</a> took only 10% of the seats, the populace was content with the selection of the delegates.<sup id="cite_ref-byind_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byind-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Belarus declared itself sovereign on <span class="nowrap">27 July</span> 1990 by issuing the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_State_Sovereignty_of_the_Belarusian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Declaration of State Sovereignty of the Belarusian Soviet Socialist Republic">Declaration of State Sovereignty of the Belarusian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>.\n</p><p>With the support of the Communist Party, the country\'s name was changed to the Republic of Belarus on <span class="nowrap">25 August</span> 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-byind_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byind-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stanislau_Shushkevich" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanislau Shushkevich">Stanislav Shushkevich</a>, the chairman of the Supreme Soviet of Belarus, met with <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a> of Russia and <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kravchuk" title="Leonid Kravchuk">Leonid Kravchuk</a> of Ukraine on <span class="nowrap">8 December</span> 1991 in <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Bia\xc5\x82owie\xc5\xbca Forest">Belavezhskaya Pushcha</a> to formally declare the dissolution of the Soviet Union and the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-byind_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byind-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Belarus" title="Constitution of Belarus">national constitution</a> was adopted in March 1994 in which the functions of prime minister were given to the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Belarus" title="President of Belarus">President of Belarus</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence">Post-independence</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Lukashenko,_opening_of_Slavianski_Bazar_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Alexander_Lukashenko%2C_opening_of_Slavianski_Bazar_2014.jpg/220px-Alexander_Lukashenko%2C_opening_of_Slavianski_Bazar_2014.jpg" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Alexander_Lukashenko%2C_opening_of_Slavianski_Bazar_2014.jpg/330px-Alexander_Lukashenko%2C_opening_of_Slavianski_Bazar_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Alexander_Lukashenko%2C_opening_of_Slavianski_Bazar_2014.jpg/440px-Alexander_Lukashenko%2C_opening_of_Slavianski_Bazar_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3578" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Lukashenko,_opening_of_Slavianski_Bazar_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lukashenko" title="Alexander Lukashenko">Alexander Lukashenko</a> has ruled Belarus since 1994, and is <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>\'s longest currently ruling elected <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of state">head of state</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Two-round elections for the presidency on (<span class="nowrap">24 June</span> 1994 and <span class="nowrap">10 July</span> 1994)<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> catapulted the formerly unknown <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lukashenko" title="Alexander Lukashenko">Alexander Lukashenko</a> into national prominence. He garnered 45% of the vote in the first round and 80%<sup id="cite_ref-byind_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byind-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> in the second, defeating <a href="/wiki/Vyachaslau_Kebich" class="mw-redirect" title="Vyachaslau Kebich">Vyacheslav Kebich</a> who received 14% of the vote. Lukashenko was re-elected <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_presidential_election,_2001" title="Belarusian presidential election, 2001">in 2001</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_presidential_election,_2006" title="Belarusian presidential election, 2006">in 2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_presidential_election,_2010" title="Belarusian presidential election, 2010">in 2010</a> and again <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_presidential_election,_2015" title="Belarusian presidential election, 2015">in 2015</a>. Western governments,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a><sup id="cite_ref-HRW_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> have criticized Lukashenko\'s <a href="/wiki/Authoritarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> style of government.\n</p><p>Since 2014, following years of embrace of Russian influence in the country, Lukashenko has pressed a revival of Belarusian identity, following the Russian <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_Ukraine_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Russian military intervention in Ukraine (2014\xe2\x80\x93present)">military intervention in Eastern Ukraine</a>. For the first time, he delivered a speech in <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a> (rather than Russian, which most people use), in which he said, "We are not Russian\xe2\x80\x94we are Belarusians", and later encouraged the use of Belarusian. Trade disputes, a border dispute, and a much relaxed official attitude to dissident voices are all part of a weakening of the longtime warm relationship with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Belarus" title="Geography of Belarus">Geography of Belarus</a></div>\n<p>Belarus lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/51st_parallel_north" title="51st parallel north">51\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/57th_parallel_north" title="57th parallel north">57\xc2\xb0 N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/23rd_meridian_east" title="23rd meridian east">23\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/33rd_meridian_east" title="33rd meridian east">33\xc2\xb0 E</a>. Its extension from north to south is 560&#160;km (350&#160;mi), from west to east is 650&#160;km (400&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-statistics_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> It is <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked</a>, relatively flat, and contains large tracts of <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">marshy</a> land.<sup id="cite_ref-ciageo_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciageo-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> About 40% of Belarus is covered by forests.<sup id="cite_ref-key_facts_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-key_facts-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many streams and 11,000 lakes are found in Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-ciageo_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciageo-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Three major rivers run through the country: the <a href="/wiki/Neman_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Neman River">Neman</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pripyat_River" title="Pripyat River">Pripyat</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dnieper_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnieper River">Dnieper</a>. The Neman flows westward towards the Baltic sea and the Pripyat flows eastward to the Dnieper; the Dnieper flows southward towards the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bell_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bell-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Strusta_Lake_-_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Strusta_Lake_-_Panorama.jpg/220px-Strusta_Lake_-_Panorama.jpg" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Strusta_Lake_-_Panorama.jpg/330px-Strusta_Lake_-_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Strusta_Lake_-_Panorama.jpg/440px-Strusta_Lake_-_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4500" data-file-height="2136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Strusta_Lake_-_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Strusta_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Strusta Lake">Strusta Lake</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Vitebsk_Region" title="Vitebsk Region">Vitebsk Region</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Dzyarzhynskaya_Hara" title="Dzyarzhynskaya Hara">Dzyarzhynskaya Hara</a> (Dzyarzhynsk Hill) at 345 metres (1,132&#160;ft), and the lowest point is on the Neman River at 90&#160;m (295&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-ciageo_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciageo-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The average elevation of Belarus is 160&#160;m (525&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The climate features mild to cold winters, with average January minimum temperatures ranging from \xe2\x88\x924&#160;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">\xc2\xb0C</a> (24.8&#160;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">\xc2\xb0F</a>) in southwest (<a href="/wiki/Brest,_Belarus" title="Brest, Belarus">Brest</a>) to \xe2\x88\x928&#160;\xc2\xb0C (17.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in northeast (<a href="/wiki/Vitebsk" title="Vitebsk">Vitebsk</a>), and cool and moist summers with an average temperature of 18&#160;\xc2\xb0C (64.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-locclimate_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-locclimate-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Belarus has an average annual rainfall of 550 to 700&#160;mm (21.7 to 27.6&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-locclimate_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-locclimate-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The country is in the transitional zone between <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ciageo_87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciageo-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Natural resources include <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> deposits, small quantities of oil and natural gas, <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a>, dolomite (<a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>), <a href="/wiki/Marl" title="Marl">marl</a>, chalk, sand, gravel, and clay.<sup id="cite_ref-ciageo_87-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciageo-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> About 70% of the radiation from neighboring Ukraine\'s 1986 <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">Chernobyl nuclear disaster</a> entered Belarusian territory, and about a fifth of Belarusian land (principally farmland and forests in the southeastern regions) was affected by radiation fallout.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The United Nations and other agencies have aimed to reduce the level of radiation in affected areas, especially through the use of <a href="/wiki/Caesium" title="Caesium">caesium</a> binders and <a href="/wiki/Rapeseed" title="Rapeseed">rapeseed</a> cultivation, which are meant to decrease soil levels of <a href="/wiki/Caesium-137" title="Caesium-137">caesium-137</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uncher_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uncher-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iaea_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iaea-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belarus borders five countries: <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> to the north and the east, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> to the south. Treaties in 1995 and 1996 demarcated Belarus\'s borders with Latvia and Lithuania, and Belarus ratified a 1997 treaty establishing the Belarus-Ukraine border in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Belarus and Lithuania ratified final border demarcation documents in February 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin:auto;">\n<caption>Average daily maximum and minimum temperatures for the six largest cities in Belarus<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Location\n</th>\n<th>July (\xc2\xb0C)\n</th>\n<th>July (\xc2\xb0F)\n</th>\n<th>January (\xc2\xb0C)\n</th>\n<th>January (\xc2\xb0F)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a></td>\n<td>23/14</td>\n<td>74/57</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x922/\xe2\x88\x926</td>\n<td>28/20\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gomel" title="Gomel">Gomel</a></td>\n<td>25/15</td>\n<td>77/58</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x922/\xe2\x88\x927</td>\n<td>28/19\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mogilev" title="Mogilev">Mogilev</a></td>\n<td>23/12</td>\n<td>74/55</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x921/\xe2\x88\x926</td>\n<td>30/21\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vitebsk" title="Vitebsk">Vitebsk</a></td>\n<td>23/13</td>\n<td>74/56</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x923/\xe2\x88\x927</td>\n<td>26/18\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Grodno" title="Grodno">Grodno</a></td>\n<td>24/12</td>\n<td>75/55</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x921/\xe2\x88\x926</td>\n<td>30/21\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Brest,_Belarus" title="Brest, Belarus">Brest</a></td>\n<td>25/14</td>\n<td>83/61</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x920/\xe2\x88\x925</td>\n<td>31/23\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Belarus" title="Politics of Belarus">Politics of Belarus</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg/220px-House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg/330px-House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg/440px-House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="663" /></a>  <div
