class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus" title="House of Representatives of Belarus">House of Representatives of Belarus</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victory_square,_Minsk_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg/220px-Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg/330px-Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg/440px-Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victory_square,_Minsk_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Victory_Square,_Minsk" title="Victory Square, Minsk">Victory Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Belarus is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> republic, governed by a <a href="/wiki/President_of_Belarus" title="President of Belarus">president</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Belarus" title="National Assembly of Belarus">National Assembly</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Term_of_office" title="Term of office">term</a> for each presidency is five years. Under the 1994 constitution, the president could serve for only two terms as president, but a <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_referendum,_2004" title="Belarusian referendum, 2004">change in the constitution in 2004</a> eliminated term limits.<sup id="cite_ref-bbclukapro_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbclukapro-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lukashenko" title="Alexander Lukashenko">Alexander Lukashenko</a> has been the president of Belarus since 1994. In 1996, Lukashenko called for a controversial vote to extend the presidential term from five to seven years, and as a result <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_presidential_election,_2001" title="Belarusian presidential election, 2001">the election</a> that was supposed to occur in 1999 was pushed back to 2001. The <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_referendum,_1996" title="Belarusian referendum, 1996">referendum on the extension</a> was denounced as a "fantastic" fake by the chief electoral officer, <a href="/wiki/Viktar_Hanchar" title="Viktar Hanchar">Viktar Hanchar</a>, who was removed from the office for official matters only during the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The National Assembly is a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral parliament</a> comprising the 110-member <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus" title="House of Representatives of Belarus">House of Representatives</a> (the lower house) and the 64-member <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Republic_of_Belarus" title="Council of the Republic of Belarus">Council of the Republic</a> (the upper house).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The House of Representatives has the power to appoint the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belarusian_Prime_Ministers" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Belarusian Prime Ministers">prime minister</a>, make constitutional amendments, call for a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_Confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="Motion of Confidence">vote of confidence</a> on the prime minister, and make suggestions on foreign and domestic policy.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The Council of the Republic has the power to select various government officials, conduct an impeachment trial of the president, and accept or reject the bills passed by the House of Representatives. Each chamber has the ability to veto any law passed by local officials if it is contrary to the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-conby_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conby-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government includes a Council of Ministers, headed by the prime minister and five deputy prime ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The members of this council need not be members of the legislature and are appointed by the president. The judiciary comprises the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Belarus" title="Supreme Court of Belarus">Supreme Court</a> and specialized courts such as the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Belarus" title="Constitutional Court of Belarus">Constitutional Court</a>, which deals with specific issues related to constitutional and business law. The judges of national courts are appointed by the president and confirmed by the Council of the Republic. For criminal cases, the highest court of appeal is the Supreme Court. The Belarusian Constitution forbids the use of special extrajudicial courts.<sup id="cite_ref-conby_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conby-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_parliamentary_election,_2012" title="Belarusian parliamentary election, 2012">2012 parliamentary election</a>, 105 of the 110 members elected to the House of Representatives were not affiliated with any political party. The <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Belarus" title="Communist Party of Belarus">Communist Party of Belarus</a> won 3 seats, and the <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_Party_(Belarus)" title="Agrarian Party (Belarus)">Agrarian Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_of_Labour_and_Justice" title="Republican Party of Labour and Justice">Republican Party of Labour and Justice</a>, one each.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Most non-partisans represent a wide scope of social organizations such as workers\' collectives, public associations, and civil society organizations, similar to the composition of the Soviet legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_controversies">Election controversies</span></h3>\n<p>Neither the pro-Lukashenko parties, such as the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Socialist_Sporting_Party" title="Belarusian Socialist Sporting Party">Belarusian Socialist Sporting Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_of_Labour_and_Justice" title="Republican Party of Labour and Justice">Republican Party of Labour and Justice</a>, nor the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Coalition_5_Plus" title="People&#39;s Coalition 5 Plus">People\'s Coalition 5 Plus</a> opposition parties, such as the <a href="/wiki/Partyja_BPF" class="mw-redirect" title="Partyja BPF">Belarusian People\'s Front</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Civil_Party_of_Belarus" class="mw-redirect" title="United Civil Party of Belarus">United Civil Party of Belarus</a>, won any seats in the <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Belarus#Elections_of_2004" title="Elections in Belarus">2004 elections</a>. Groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) declared the election "un-free" because of the opposition parties\' poor results and media bias in favor of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-OSCE_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSCE-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_presidential_election,_2006" title="Belarusian presidential election, 2006">2006 presidential election</a>, Lukashenko was opposed by <a href="/wiki/Alaksandar_Milinkievi%C4%8D" title="Alaksandar Milinkievi\xc4\x8d">Alaksandar Milinkievi\xc4\x8d</a>, who represented a coalition of opposition parties, and by <a href="/wiki/Alaksandar_Kazulin" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaksandar Kazulin">Alaksandar Kazulin</a> of the Social Democrats. Kazulin was detained and beaten by police during protests surrounding the <a href="/wiki/All_Belarusian_People%27s_Assembly" title="All Belarusian People&#39;s Assembly">All Belarusian People\'s Assembly</a>. Lukashenko won the election with 80% of the vote; the Russian Federation and the CIS deemed the vote open and fair<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> while the OSCE and other organizations called the election unfair.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the December completion of the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_presidential_election,_2010" title="Belarusian presidential election, 2010">2010 presidential election</a>, Lukashenko was elected to a fourth straight term with nearly 80% of the vote in elections. The runner-up opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Sannikov" title="Andrei Sannikov">Andrei Sannikov</a> received less than 3% of the vote; independent observers criticized the election as fraudulent. When opposition protesters took to the streets in <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, many people, including most rival presidential candidates, were beaten and arrested by the state militia.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Many of the candidates, including Sannikov, were sentenced to prison or house arrest for terms which are mainly and typically over four years.<sup id="cite_ref-SannikovSentenced_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SannikovSentenced-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kyi_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kyi-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Six months later amid an unprecedented economic crisis, activists utilized social networking to initiate a fresh round of protests characterized by wordless hand-clapping.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span></h3>\n<p>The judicial system in Belarus lacks independence and is subject to political interference.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Corrupt practices such as bribery often took place during tender processes, and <a href="/wiki/Whistleblower" title="Whistleblower">whistleblower</a> protection and national <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">ombudsman</a> are lacking in Belarus\'s anti-corruption system.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> However, there is a political will to fight against corruption in the government, and the government has made some progress in combating corruption, such as minimizing tax regulations in order to improve transparency in the tax office.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Belarus" title="Human rights in Belarus">Human rights in Belarus</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg/220px-Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg/330px-Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg/440px-Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag which served as the national flag in 1918 and from 1991 to 1995. Actively used by Belarusian opposition nowadays.</div></div></div>\n<p>Lukashenko has described himself as having an "authoritarian ruling style".<sup id="cite_ref-bbclukapro_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbclukapro-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Western countries have described Belarus under Lukashenko as a dictatorship; the government has accused the same Western powers of trying to oust Lukashenko.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> has barred Belarus from membership since 1997 for undemocratic voting and election irregularities in the November 1996 constitutional referendum and parliament by-elections.<sup id="cite_ref-CoE_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CoE-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Belarusian government is also criticized for human rights violations and its persecution of non-governmental organisations, independent journalists, national minorities, and opposition politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRW_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In a testimony to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Foreign_Relations" title="United States Senate Committee on Foreign Relations">United States Senate Committee on Foreign Relations</a>, former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> labeled Belarus as one of the world\'s six "<a href="/wiki/Outposts_of_tyranny" title="Outposts of tyranny">outposts of tyranny</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In response, the Belarusian government called the assessment "quite far from reality".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Viasna_Human_Rights_Centre" title="Viasna Human Rights Centre">Viasna Human Rights Centre</a> lists 11 political prisoners<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> currently detained in Belarus. Among them is the human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Ales_Bialiatski" title="Ales Bialiatski">Ales Bialiatski</a>, Vice President of <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_for_Human_Rights" title="International Federation for Human Rights">International Federation for Human Rights</a> and head of Viasna.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lukashenko announced a new law in 2014 that will prohibit <a href="/wiki/Kolkhoz" title="Kolkhoz">kolkhoz</a> workers (around 9% of total work force) from leaving their jobs at will\xe2\x80\x94a change of job and living location will require permission from governors. The law was compared with <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">serfdom</a> by Lukashenko himself.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Similar regulations were introduced for the forestry industry in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Belarus" title="Foreign relations of Belarus">Foreign relations of Belarus</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CSTO_Collective_Security_Council_meeting_Kremlin,_Moscow_2012-12-19_01.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/CSTO_Collective_Security_Council_meeting_Kremlin%2C_Moscow_2012-12-19_01.jpeg/220px-CSTO_Collective_Security_Council_meeting_Kremlin%2C_Moscow_2012-12-19_01.jpeg" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/CSTO_Collective_Security_Council_meeting_Kremlin%2C_Moscow_2012-12-19_01.jpeg/330px-CSTO_Collective_Security_Council_meeting_Kremlin%2C_Moscow_2012-12-19_01.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/CSTO_Collective_Security_Council_meeting_Kremlin%2C_Moscow_2012-12-19_01.jpeg/440px-CSTO_Collective_Security_Council_meeting_Kremlin%2C_Moscow_2012-12-19_01.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CSTO_Collective_Security_Council_meeting_Kremlin,_Moscow_2012-12-19_01.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lukashenko" title="Alexander Lukashenko">Alexander Lukashenko</a>, right, shaking hands with <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">Russian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, left, in 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>The Byelorussian SSR was one of the two Soviet republics that joined the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> along with the Ukrainian SSR as one of the original 51 members in 1945. After the dissolution of the Soviet Union, under international law, Belarus became the internationally recognized successor state to the Byelorussian SSR, retaining its UN membership.\n</p><p>Belarus and Russia have been close trading partners and diplomatic allies since the breakup of the Soviet Union. Belarus is dependent on Russia for imports of raw materials and for its export market.<sup id="cite_ref-stategov_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stategov-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Russia_and_Belarus" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Russia and Belarus">union of Russia and Belarus</a>, a supranational confederation, was established in a 1996\xe2\x80\x9399 series of treaties that called for monetary union, equal rights, single citizenship, and a common foreign and defense policy.<sup id="cite_ref-stategov_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stategov-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> However, the future of the union has been placed in doubt because of Belarus\'s repeated delays of monetary union, the lack of a referendum date for the draft constitution, and a <a href="/wiki/2007_Russia%E2%80%93Belarus_energy_dispute" title="2007 Russia\xe2\x80\x93Belarus energy dispute">dispute over the petroleum trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stategov_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stategov-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 December 2007, reports emerged that a framework for the new state was discussed between both countries.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> On <span class="nowrap">27 May</span> 2008, Belarusian President Lukashenko said that he had named <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Russia" title="Prime Minister of Russia">Russian Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> the "prime minister" of the Russia-Belarus alliance. The significance of this act was not immediately clear; some incorrectly speculated that Putin would become president of a unified state of Russia and Belarus after stepping down as Russian president in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belarus was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS).<sup id="cite_ref-cisstrained_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cisstrained-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Belarus has trade agreements with several <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states (despite other member states\' travel ban on Lukashenko and top officials),<sup id="cite_ref-euban_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euban-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> including neighboring Latvia, Lithuania, and Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-foreignrelations_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreignrelations-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Travel bans imposed by the European Union have been lifted in the past in order to allow Lukashenko to attend diplomatic meetings and also to engage his government and opposition groups in dialogue.<sup id="cite_ref-Belarus_president_visits_Vatican_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belarus_president_visits_Vatican-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_(February_2015)_03.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg/220px-Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg/330px-Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg/440px-Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_(February_2015)_03.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leaders of Belarus, Russia, Germany, France, and Ukraine at the summit in <a href="/wiki/Minsk_II" title="Minsk II">Minsk</a>, 11\xe2\x80\x9312 February 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>Bilateral relations with the United States are strained because the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. Department of State</a> supports various anti-Lukashenko non-governmental organizations (NGOs), and also because the Belarusian government has made it increasingly difficult for United States-based organizations to operate within the country.<sup id="cite_ref-fy97_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fy97-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Diplomatic relations remained tense, and in 2004, the United States passed the <a href="/wiki/Belarus_Democracy_Act_of_2004" title="Belarus Democracy Act of 2004">Belarus Democracy Act</a>, which authorized funding for anti-government Belarusian NGOs, and prohibited loans to the Belarusian government, except for humanitarian purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Despite this political friction, the two countries do cooperate on intellectual property protection, prevention of human trafficking, technology crime, and disaster relief.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sino-Belarusian relations have improved,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> strengthened by the visit of President Lukashenko to China in October 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Belarus also has strong ties with <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> considered a key partner in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the CIS, Belarus is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Community" title="Eurasian Economic Community">Eurasian Economic Community</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">Collective Security Treaty Organisation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-foreignrelations_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreignrelations-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> the international <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> since 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-byintorgs_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byintorgs-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_on_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization on Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization on Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE). As an OSCE member state, Belarus\'s international commitments are subject to monitoring under the mandate of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Helsinki_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Helsinki Commission">U.S. Helsinki Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belarus is included in the European Union\'s <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> (ENP) which aims at bringing the EU and its neighbours closer.\n</p><p>On 15 February 2016 the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> announced the easing of sanctions against Belarus during a meeting by 28 EU foreign ministers at a regular session of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Russian_News_Agency_TASS_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russian_News_Agency_TASS-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Belarus" title="Armed Forces of Belarus">Armed Forces of Belarus</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="585" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soldiers patrol in the <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Bia\xc5\x82owie\xc5\xbca Forest">Bia\xc5\x82owie\xc5\xbca Forest</a> on the Belarusian border with Poland.</div></div></div>\n<p>Major General <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Ravkov" title="Andrei Ravkov">Andrei Ravkov</a> heads the Ministry of Defence,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and Alexander Lukashenko (as president) serves as Commander-in-Chief.<sup id="cite_ref-conby_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conby-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The armed forces were formed in 1992 using parts of the former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Armed_Forces" title="Soviet Armed Forces">Soviet Armed Forces</a> on the new republic\'s territory. The transformation of the ex-Soviet forces into the Armed Forces of Belarus, which was completed in 1997, reduced the number of its soldiers by 30,000 and restructured its leadership and military formations.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of Belarus\'s service members are <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscripts</a>, who serve for 12 months if they have higher education or 18 months if they do not.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Demographic decreases in the Belarusians of conscription age have increased the importance of contract soldiers, who numbered 12,000 in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-conscripts_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conscripts-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, about 1.4% of Belarus\'s gross domestic product was devoted to military expenditure.<sup id="cite_ref-ciabymil_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciabymil-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belarus has not expressed a desire to join <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> but has participated in the Individual Partnership Program since 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> and Belarus provides refueling and airspace support for the <a href="/wiki/ISAF" class="mw-redirect" title="ISAF">ISAF</a> mission in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Belarus first began to cooperate with NATO upon signing documents to participate in their Partnership for Peace Program in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> However, Belarus cannot join NATO because it is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">Collective Security Treaty Organisation</a>. Tensions between NATO and Belarus peaked after the March 2006 presidential election in Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Belarus" title="Regions of Belarus">Regions of Belarus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Belarus" title="Districts of Belarus">Districts of Belarus</a></div>\n<p>Belarus is divided into six <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">regions</a> (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">\xd0\xb2\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x81\xd1\x86\xd1\x8c</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">\xd0\xbe\xcc\x81\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x81\xd1\x82\xd1\x8c</span>), which are named after the cities that serve as their administrative centers.<sup id="cite_ref-s1_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Each region has a provincial legislative authority, called a region council (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x81\xd0\xbd\xd1\x8b \xd0\xa1\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb5\xd1\x82 \xd0\x94\xd1\x8d\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd1\x82\xd0\xb0\xd1\x82\xd0\xb0\xd1\x9e</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x81\xd1\x82\xd0\xbd\xd0\xbe\xcc\x81\xd0\xb9 \xd0\xa1\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb5\xcc\x81\xd1\x82 \xd0\x94\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd1\x82\xd0\xb0\xd1\x82\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2</span>), which is elected by its residents, and a provincial executive authority called a region administration (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x81\xd0\xbd\xd1\x8b \xd0\xb2\xd1\x8b\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0\xd1\x9e\xd1\x87\xd1\x8b \xd0\xba\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbc\xd1\x96\xd1\x82\xd1\x8d\xd1\x82</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd1\x81\xd1\x82\xd0\xbd\xd0\xbe\xcc\x81\xd0\xb9 \xd0\xb8\xd1\x81\xd0\xbf\xd0\xbe\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb8\xd1\x82\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd1\x8c\xd0\xbd\xd1\x8b\xd0\xb9 \xd0\xba\xd0\xbe\xd0\xbc\xd0\xb8\xd1\x82\xd0\xb5\xcc\x81\xd1\x82</span>), whose chairman is appointed by the president.<sup id="cite_ref-s5_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s5-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Regions are further subdivided into <i><a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">raions</a></i>, commonly translated as <i>districts</i> (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">\xd1\x80\xd0\xb0\xd1\x91\xd0\xbd</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">\xd1\x80\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb9\xd0\xbe\xd0\xbd</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-s1_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Each <i>raion</i> has its own legislative authority, or <i>raion</i> council, (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">\xd1\x80\xd0\xb0\xd1\x91\xd0\xbd\xd0\xbd\xd1\x8b \xd0\xa1\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb5\xd1\x82 \xd0\x94\xd1\x8d\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd1\x82\xd0\xb0\xd1\x82\xd0\xb0\xd1\x9e</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">\xd1\x80\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb9\xd0\xbe\xd0\xbd\xd0\xbd\xd1\x8b\xd0\xb9 \xd0\xa1\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb5\xcc\x81\xd1\x82 \xd0\x94\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbf\xd1\x83\xd1\x82\xd0\xb0\xd1\x82\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2</span>) elected by its residents, and an executive authority or <i>raion</i> administration appointed by higher executive powers. The six regions are divided into 118 <i>raions</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-key_facts_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-key_facts-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city of Minsk is split into nine districts and enjoys special status as the nation\'s capital.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> It is run by an executive committee and has been granted a charter of self-rule.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Regions (with administrative centers):</b>\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Brest_Region" title="Brest Region">Brest Region</a> (<a href="/wiki/Brest,_Belarus" title="Brest, Belarus">Brest</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gomel_Region" title="Gomel Region">Gomel Region</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gomel" title="Gomel">Gomel</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Grodno_Region" title="Grodno Region">Grodno Region</a> (<a href="/wiki/Grodno" title="Grodno">Grodno</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mogilev_Region" title="Mogilev Region">Mogilev Region</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mogilev" title="Mogilev">Mogilev</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Minsk_Region" title="Minsk Region">Minsk Region</a> (<a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vitebsk_Region" title="Vitebsk Region">Vitebsk Region</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vitebsk" title="Vitebsk">Vitebsk</a>)</li></ol>\n<p><b>Special administrative district:</b>\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk City</a></li></ol>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_punishment"><span id="Death_penalty"></span>Capital punishment</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Belarus" title="Capital punishment in Belarus">Capital punishment in Belarus</a></div>\n<p>Belarus is the only European country still using <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">capital punishment</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_United_States" title="Human rights in the United States">U.S.</a> and Belarus were the only two of the 56 member states of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> to have carried out executions during 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg/310px-Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg" width="310" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg/465px-Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg/620px-Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="924" data-file-height="719" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A graphical depiction of Belarus\'s product exports in 28&#160;colour-coded categories</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg/310px-Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg" width="310" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg/465px-Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg/620px-Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1383" data-file-height="877" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Belarusian annual GDP and CPI rates 2001\xe2\x80\x932013</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Belarus" title="Economy of Belarus">Economy of Belarus</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span></h3>\n<p>In 2014 the share of manufacturing in GDP was 37%, more than two thirds of this amount falls on manufacturing industries. The number of people employed in industry is 32.7% of the working population. The growth rate is much lower than for the economy as a whole \xe2\x80\x93 about 1.9% in 2014.\n</p><p>At the time of the dissolution of the Soviet Union in 1991, Belarus was one of the world\'s most industrially developed states by percentage of GDP as well as the richest CIS member-state.<sup id="cite_ref-wb97_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb97-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, 39.3% of Belarusians were employed by state-controlled companies, 57.2% were employed by private companies (in which the government has a 21.1% stake) and 3.5% were employed by foreign companies.<sup id="cite_ref-econstats_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econstats-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The country relies on Russia for various imports, including petroleum.<sup id="cite_ref-natotrade_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natotrade-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Important agricultural products include potatoes and cattle byproducts, including meat.<sup id="cite_ref-ciaecon_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciaecon-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In 1994, Belarus\'s main exports included heavy machinery (especially <a href="/wiki/Belarus_(tractor)" title="Belarus (tractor)">tractors</a>), agricultural products, and energy products.<sup id="cite_ref-byexports_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byexports-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\nEconomically, Belarus involved itself in the CIS, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Community" title="Eurasian Economic Community">Eurasian Economic Community</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Union_State" title="Union State">Union with Russia</a>.\n</p><p>In the 1990s, however, industrial production plunged due to decreases in imports, investment, and demand for Belarusian products from its trading partners.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> GDP only began to rise in 1996;<sup id="cite_ref-bybriefwb06_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bybriefwb06-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> the country was the fastest-recovering former Soviet republic in the terms of its economy.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, GDP amounted to <span class="nowrap">US$83.1 billion</span> in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) dollars (estimate), or about $8,100 per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-ciaecon_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciaecon-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, GDP increased by 9.9%; the inflation rate averaged 9.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-ciaecon_161-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciaecon-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the disintegration of the Soviet Union, under Lukashenko\'s leadership, Belarus has maintained government control over key industries and eschewed the large-scale privatizations seen in other former Soviet republics.\n</p><p>In 2006, Belarus\'s largest trading partner was Russia, accounting for nearly half of total trade, with the European Union the next largest trading partner, with nearly a third of foreign trade.<sup id="cite_ref-tradestats_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tradestats-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eutrade_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eutrade-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> As of 2015, 38% of Belarusian exported goods go to Russia and 56% of imported goods come from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-econstats_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econstats-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to its failure to protect labor rights, including passing laws forbidding unemployment or working outside of state-controlled sectors,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Belarus lost its EU <a href="/wiki/Generalized_System_of_Preferences" title="Generalized System of Preferences">Generalized System of Preferences</a> status on <span class="nowrap">21 June</span> 2007, which raised tariff rates to their prior <a href="/wiki/Most_favored_nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Most favored nation">most favored nation</a> levels.<sup id="cite_ref-eutrade_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eutrade-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Belarus applied to become a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The labor force consists of more than four million people, among whom women hold slightly more jobs than men.<sup id="cite_ref-econstats_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econstats-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, nearly a quarter of the population was employed by industrial factories. Employment is also high in agriculture, manufacturing sales, trading goods, and education. The unemployment rate, according to government statistics, was 1.5% in 2005. There were 679,000 unemployed Belarusians, two-thirds of whom were women. The unemployment rate has been in decline since 2003, and the overall rate of employment is the highest since statistics were first compiled in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-econstats_158-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econstats-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Until 1 July 2016, the currency of Belarus was the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_ruble" title="Belarusian ruble">Belarusian ruble</a> (BYR). The currency was introduced in May 1992, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_ruble" title="Soviet ruble">Soviet ruble</a>. The first coins of the Republic of Belarus were issued on 27 December 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The ruble was reintroduced with new values in 2000 and has been in use ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> As part of the <a href="/wiki/Union_State" title="Union State">Union of Russia and Belarus</a>, both states have discussed using a single currency along the same lines as the Euro. This led to a proposal that the Belarusian ruble be discontinued in favor of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> (RUB), starting as early as <span class="nowrap">1 January</span> 2008. The <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_the_Republic_of_Belarus" title="National Bank of the Republic of Belarus">National Bank of Belarus</a> abandoned pegging the Belarusian ruble to the Russian ruble in August 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A new currency, the <a href="/wiki/New_Belarusian_ruble" class="mw-redirect" title="New Belarusian ruble">new Belarusian ruble</a> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> code: BYN)<sup id="cite_ref-currency-iso.org_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currency-iso.org-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> was introduced in July 2016, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_ruble" title="Belarusian ruble">Belarusian ruble</a> in a rate of 1:10,000 (10,000 old rubles = 1 new ruble). From 1 July until 31 December 2016, the old and new currencies will be in parallel circulation and series 2000 notes and coins can be exchanged for series 2009 from 1 January 2017 to 31 December 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-currency-iso.org_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currency-iso.org-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Redenomination" title="Redenomination">redenomination</a> can be considered an effort to fight the high inflation rate.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The banking system of Belarus consists of two levels: Central Bank (National Bank of the Republic of Belarus) and 25 commercial banks.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> On 23 May 2011, the Belarusian ruble depreciated 56% against the United States dollar. The depreciation was even steeper on the black market and financial collapse seemed imminent as citizens rushed to exchange their rubles for dollars, euros, durable goods, and canned goods.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> On 1 June 2011, Belarus requested an economic rescue package from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px"><div style="width: 182px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:BelAZ_75600.JPG" class="image"><img data-file-height="1944" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>MOAZ-6014 Scraper\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Belarus" title="Demographics of Belarus">Demographics of Belarus</a></div>\n<p>According to the National Statistical Committee, as of January 2016, the population is 9.49 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-2009census_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009census-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Ethnic <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a> constitute 83.7% of Belarus\'s total population.<sup id="cite_ref-2009census_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009census-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The next largest ethnic groups are: <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (8.3%), <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> (3.1%), and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> (1.7%).<sup id="cite_ref-2009census_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009census-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\nBelarus has a population density of about 50 people per square kilometer (127 per sq&#160;mi); 70% of its total population is concentrated in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, the nation\'s capital and largest city, was home to 1,937,900 residents in 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belarus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gomel" title="Gomel">Gomel</a>, with a population of 481,000, is the second-largest city and serves as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Homiel_Voblast" class="mw-redirect" title="Homiel Voblast">Homiel Voblast</a>. Other large cities are <a href="/wiki/Mogilev" title="Mogilev">Mogilev</a> (365,100), <a href="/wiki/Vitebsk" title="Vitebsk">Vitebsk</a> (342,400), <a href="/wiki/Hrodna" class="mw-redirect" title="Hrodna">Hrodna</a> (314,800) and <a href="/wiki/Brest,_Belarus" title="Brest, Belarus">Brest</a> (298,300).<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Like many other eastern European countries, Belarus has a negative population growth rate and a negative natural growth rate. In 2007, Belarus\'s population declined by 0.41% and its <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">fertility rate</a> was 1.22,<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> well <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">below the replacement rate</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Net_migration_rate" title="Net migration rate">net migration rate</a> is +0.38 per 1,000, indicating that Belarus experiences slightly more immigration than emigration. As of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belarus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 69.9% of Belarus\'s population is aged 14 to 64; 15.5% is under 14, and 14.6% is 65 or older. Its population is also aging; the median age of 30\xe2\x80\x9334 is estimated to rise to between 60 and 64 in 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> There are about 0.87 males per female in Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The average life expectancy is 72.15 (66.53 years for men and 78.1 years for women).<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Over 99% of Belarusians aged 15 and older are <a href="/wiki/Literate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literate">literate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_184-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<table class="navbox">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title"><div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style="float: Belarus">Region</a>\n</th>\n<th>Pop.\n</th>\n<th>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="11" style="text-align: center"><a href="/wiki/File:Miensk_-_Plac_Niezale%C5%BEna%C5%9Bci.jpg" class="image" style="text-align:right;">144,945\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Pinsk" title="Pinsk">Pinsk</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Brest_Voblast" class="mw-redirect" title="Brest Voblast">Brest Voblast</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">137,493\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Belarus" title="Languages of Belarus">Languages of Belarus</a></div>\n<p>Belarus\'s two official languages are Russian and <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Russian is the main language, used by 72% of the population, while Belarusian, the official first language, is spoken by 11.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Minorities also speak <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Yiddish" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Yiddish">Eastern Yiddish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Belarusian, although not as widely used as Russian, is the mother tongue of 53.2% of the population, whereas Russian is the mother tongue of only 41.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Belarus" title="Religion in Belarus">Religion in Belarus</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:none"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Belarus (2011)<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup></th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodoxy</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:DeepPink; width:48.3%; overflow: colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Roman Catholicism</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div
