colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other religions</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:LimeGreen; width:3.3%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3.3%</td>\n</tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/225px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" width="225" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/338px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/450px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg 2x" data-file-width="714" data-file-height="562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Saint_Sophia_Cathedral_in_Polotsk" title="Saint Sophia Cathedral in Polotsk">Saint Sophia Cathedral in Polotsk</a> is one of the oldest churches in Belarus. Its current style is an ideal example of <a href="/wiki/Baroque_in_Poland" title="Baroque in Poland">baroque architecture</a> in the former <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian Commonwealth</a></div></div></div>\n<p>According to the census of as of  November 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belarus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 58.9% of all Belarusians adhere to some kind of religion; out of those, <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Orthodox_Church" title="Belarusian Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodoxy</a> (Belarusian Exarchate of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>) makes up about 82%.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Belarus" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Belarus">Roman Catholicism</a> is practiced mostly in the western regions, and there are also different denominations of Protestantism.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> Minorities also practice <a href="/wiki/Greek_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Catholicism">Greek Catholicism</a>, Judaism, Islam and Neopaganism. Overall, 48.3% of the population is Orthodox Christian, 41.1% is not religious, 7.1% is Catholic and 3.3% follows other religions.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_190-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belarus\'s Catholic minority is concentrated in the western part of the country, especially around <a href="/wiki/Hrodna" class="mw-redirect" title="Hrodna">Hrodna</a>, is made up of a mixture of Belarusians and the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithuanian people">Lithuanian</a> minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-Belarus_\xe2\x80\x93_Religion_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belarus_\xe2\x80\x93_Religion-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> In a statement to the media regarding Belarusian-Vatican ties, President Lukashenko stated that Orthodox and Catholic believers are the "two main confessions in our country".<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belarus was once a major center of European Jews, with 10% of the population being <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Belarus" title="History of the Jews in Belarus">Jewish</a>. But since the mid-20th century, the number of Jews has been reduced by the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, deportation, and emigration, so that today it is a very small minority of less than one percent.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lipka_Tatars" title="Lipka Tatars">Lipka Tatars</a>, numbering over 15,000, are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Belarus" title="Islam in Belarus">Muslims</a>. According to Article 16 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Belarus" title="Constitution of Belarus">Constitution</a>, Belarus has no official religion. While the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of worship</a> is granted in the same article, religious organizations deemed harmful to the government or social order can be prohibited.<sup id="cite_ref-s1_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Belarus" title="Culture of Belarus">Culture of Belarus</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_literature">Arts and literature</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Theatre_opera%26ballet,_Minsk.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Theatre_opera%26ballet%2C_Minsk.JPG/220px-Theatre_opera%26ballet%2C_Minsk.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Theatre_opera%26ballet%2C_Minsk.JPG/330px-Theatre_opera%26ballet%2C_Minsk.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Theatre_opera%26ballet%2C_Minsk.JPG/440px-Theatre_opera%26ballet%2C_Minsk.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Theatre_opera%26ballet,_Minsk.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Opera_and_Ballet_of_Belarus" title="National Opera and Ballet of Belarus">Opera and Ballet Theater</a> in Minsk</div></div></div>\n<p>The Belarusian government sponsors annual cultural festivals such as the <a href="/wiki/Slavianski_Bazaar_in_Vitebsk" title="Slavianski Bazaar in Vitebsk">Slavianski Bazaar in Vitebsk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> which showcases Belarusian performers, artists, writers, musicians, and actors. Several state holidays, such as <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Independence_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by Independence Day">Independence Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victory_Day_(9_May)" title="Victory Day (9 May)">Victory Day</a>, draw big crowds and often include displays such as fireworks and military parades, especially in Vitebsk and Minsk.<sup id="cite_ref-festivals_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-festivals-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The government\'s Ministry of Culture finances events promoting Belarusian arts and culture both inside and outside the country.\n</p><p>Belarusian literature<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> began with 11th- to 13th-century religious scripture, such as the 12th-century poetry of <a href="/wiki/Cyril_of_Turaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyril of Turaw">Cyril of Turaw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bypoem_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bypoem-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Polotsk" title="Polotsk">Polotsk</a> resident <a href="/wiki/Francysk_Skaryna" title="Francysk Skaryna">Francysk Skaryna</a> translated the Bible into Belarusian. It was published in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vilnius" title="Vilnius">Vilnius</a> sometime between 1517 and 1525, making it the first book printed in Belarus or anywhere in Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-byeb_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byeb-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The modern era of Belarusian literature began in the late 19th century; one prominent writer was <a href="/wiki/Yanka_Kupala" title="Yanka Kupala">Yanka Kupala</a>. Many Belarusian writers of the time, such as <a href="/wiki/U%C5%82adzimir_%C5%BDy%C5%82ka" title="U\xc5\x82adzimir \xc5\xbdy\xc5\x82ka">U\xc5\x82adzimir \xc5\xbdy\xc5\x82ka</a>, Kazimir Svayak, <a href="/wiki/Yakub_Kolas" title="Yakub Kolas">Yakub Kolas</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%B9mitrok_Biadula" title="\xc5\xb9mitrok Biadula">\xc5\xb9mitrok Biadula</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maksim_Haretski" title="Maksim Haretski">Maksim Haretski</a>, wrote for <i><a href="/wiki/Nasha_Niva" title="Nasha Niva">Nasha Niva</a></i>, a Belarusian-language paper published that was previously published in Vilnius but now is published in Minsk.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg/150px-Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg" width="150" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg/225px-Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg/300px-Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="681" data-file-height="1126" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Poet and librettist <a href="/wiki/Vintsent_Dunin-Martsinkyevich" title="Vintsent Dunin-Martsinkyevich">Vintsent Dunin-Martsinkyevich</a></div></div></div>\n<p>After Belarus was incorporated into the Soviet Union, the Soviet government took control of the Republic\'s cultural affairs. At first, a policy of "Belarusianization" was followed in the newly formed Byelorussian SSR. This policy was reversed in the 1930s, and the majority of prominent Belarusian intellectuals and nationalist advocates were either exiled or killed in Stalinist purges.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The free development of literature occurred only in Polish-held territory until Soviet occupation in 1939. Several poets and authors went into exile after the Nazi occupation of Belarus and would not return until the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-byeb_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byeb-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The last major revival of Belarusian literature occurred in the 1960s with novels published by <a href="/wiki/Vasil_Byka%C5%AD" title="Vasil Byka\xc5\xad">Vasil Byka\xc5\xad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uladzimir_Karatkievich" title="Uladzimir Karatkievich">Uladzimir Karatkievich</a>. An influential author who devoted his work to awakening the awareness of the catastrophes the country has suffered, was <a href="/wiki/Ales_Adamovich" title="Ales Adamovich">Ales Adamovich</a>. He was named by <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Alexievich" title="Svetlana Alexievich">Svetlana Alexievich</a>, the Belarusian winner of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> 2015, as "her main teacher, who helped her to find a path of her own".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skaryna_1517.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Skaryna_1517.jpg/150px-Skaryna_1517.jpg" width="150" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Skaryna_1517.jpg/225px-Skaryna_1517.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Skaryna_1517.jpg/300px-Skaryna_1517.jpg 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skaryna_1517.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Francysk_Skaryna" title="Francysk Skaryna">Francysk Skaryna</a>, developer of the Belarusian language, and one of the first people to print in the <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyrillic">Cyrillic</a> alphabet</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Belarus" title="Music of Belarus">Music in Belarus</a> largely comprises a rich tradition of folk and religious music. The country\'s folk music traditions can be traced back to the times of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>. In the 19th century, Polish composer <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Moniuszko" title="Stanis\xc5\x82aw Moniuszko">Stanis\xc5\x82aw Moniuszko</a> composed operas and chamber music pieces while living in Minsk. During his stay, he worked with Belarusian poet <a href="/wiki/Vintsent_Dunin-Martsinkyevich" title="Vintsent Dunin-Martsinkyevich">Vintsent Dunin-Martsinkyevich</a> and created the opera <i>Sialanka</i> (<i>Peasant Woman</i>). At the end of the 19th century, major Belarusian cities formed their own opera and ballet companies. The ballet <i><a href="/wiki/Nightingale_(ballet)" title="Nightingale (ballet)">Nightingale</a></i> by M. Kroshner was composed during the Soviet era and became the first Belarusian ballet showcased at the National Academic Vialiki Ballet Theatre in Minsk.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, music focused on the hardships of the Belarusian people or on those who took up arms in defense of the homeland. During this period, <a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Bogatyrev" title="Anatoly Bogatyrev">Anatoly Bogatyrev</a>, creator of the opera <i>In Polesye Virgin Forest</i>, served as the "tutor" of Belarusian composers.<sup id="cite_ref-clasmus_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clasmus-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The National Academic Theatre of Ballet in Minsk was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Prix_Benois_de_la_Danse" title="Prix Benois de la Danse">Benois de la Dance Prize</a> in 1996 as the top ballet company in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-clasmus_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clasmus-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Rock music has become increasingly popular in recent years, though the Belarusian government has attempted to limit the amount of foreign music aired on the radio in favor of traditional Belarusian music. Since 2004, Belarus has been sending artists to the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Marc_Chagall" title="Marc Chagall">Marc Chagall</a> was born in Liozna (near <a href="/wiki/Vitebsk" title="Vitebsk">Vitebsk</a>) in 1887. He spent the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> years in Soviet Belarus, becoming one of the country\'s most distinguished artists and a member of the modernist <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> and was a founder of the Vitebsk Arts College.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dress">Dress</span></h3>\n<p>The traditional Belarusian dress originates from the <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus&#39;">Kievan Rus\'</a> period. Due to the cool climate, clothes were designed to preserve body heat and were usually made from <a href="/wiki/Flax" title="Flax">flax</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>. They were decorated with ornate patterns influenced by the neighboring cultures: Poles, Lithuanians, Latvians, Russians, and other European nations. Each region of Belarus has developed specific design patterns.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> One ornamental pattern common in early dresses currently decorates the hoist of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Belarus" title="Flag of Belarus">Belarusian national flag</a>, adopted in a <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_referendum,_1995" title="Belarusian referendum, 1995">disputed referendum</a> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Potato_pancakes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Potato_pancakes.jpg/220px-Potato_pancakes.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Potato_pancakes.jpg/330px-Potato_pancakes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Potato_pancakes.jpg/440px-Potato_pancakes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Potato_pancakes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Potato_pancake" title="Potato pancake">Draniki</a>, the national dish</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Belarusian_cuisine" title="Belarusian cuisine">Belarusian cuisine</a> consists mainly of vegetables, meat (particularly pork), and bread. Foods are usually either slowly cooked or <a href="/wiki/Stewed" class="mw-redirect" title="Stewed">stewed</a>. Typically, Belarusians eat a light breakfast and two hearty meals, with dinner being the largest meal of the day. <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">Wheat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rye" title="Rye">rye</a> breads are consumed in Belarus, but rye is more plentiful because conditions are too harsh for growing wheat. To show hospitality, a host traditionally presents an offering of <a href="/wiki/Bread_and_salt" title="Bread and salt">bread and salt</a> when greeting a guest or visitor.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Belarus_at_the_Olympics" title="Belarus at the Olympics">Belarus at the Olympics</a></div>\n<p>Belarus has competed in the Olympic Games since the <a href="/wiki/1994_Winter_Olympics" title="1994 Winter Olympics">1994 Winter Olympics</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committee</a> has been headed by President Lukashenko since 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Receiving heavy sponsorship from the government, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> is the nation\'s second most popular sport after <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Belarus_national_football_team" title="Belarus national football team">national football team</a> has never qualified for a major tournament; however, <a href="/wiki/FC_BATE_Borisov" title="FC BATE Borisov">BATE Borisov</a> has played in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Belarus_national_men%27s_ice_hockey_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Belarus national men&#39;s ice hockey team">national hockey team</a> finished fourth at the <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics" title="Ice hockey at the 2002 Winter Olympics">2002 Salt Lake City Olympics</a> following a memorable upset win over Sweden in the quarterfinals, and regularly competes in the <a href="/wiki/Ice_Hockey_World_Championships" title="Ice Hockey World Championships">World Championships</a>, often making the quarterfinals. Numerous Belarusian players are present in the <a href="/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League" title="Kontinental Hockey League">Kontinental Hockey League</a> in Eurasia, particularly for Belarusian club <a href="/wiki/HC_Dinamo_Minsk" title="HC Dinamo Minsk">HC Dinamo Minsk</a>, and several have also played in the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> in North America. <a href="/wiki/Darya_Domracheva" title="Darya Domracheva">Darya Domracheva</a> is a leading <a href="/wiki/Biathlon" title="Biathlon">biathlete</a> whose honours include three gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Azarenka_(18567208246).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Victoria_Azarenka_%2818567208246%29.jpg/220px-Victoria_Azarenka_%2818567208246%29.jpg" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Victoria_Azarenka_%2818567208246%29.jpg/330px-Victoria_Azarenka_%2818567208246%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Victoria_Azarenka_%2818567208246%29.jpg/440px-Victoria_Azarenka_%2818567208246%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4042" data-file-height="3541" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Azarenka_(18567208246).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Victoria_Azarenka" title="Victoria Azarenka">Victoria Azarenka</a>, professional <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> player and a former <a href="/wiki/List_of_WTA_number_1_ranked_players" class="mw-redirect" title="List of WTA number 1 ranked players">world No. 1</a> in singles</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a> player <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Azarenka" title="Victoria Azarenka">Victoria Azarenka</a> became the first Belarusian to win a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> singles title at the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Open" title="Australian Open">Australian Open</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> She also won the gold medal in mixed doubles at the <a href="/wiki/Tennis_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Tennis at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> with <a href="/wiki/Max_Mirnyi" title="Max Mirnyi">Max Mirnyi</a>, who holds ten Grand Slam titles in <a href="/wiki/Singles_tennis" class="mw-redirect" title="Singles tennis">doubles</a>.\n</p><p>Other notable Belarusian sportspeople include cyclist <a href="/wiki/Vasil_Kiryienka" title="Vasil Kiryienka">Vasil Kiryienka</a>, who won the <a href="/wiki/2015_UCI_Road_World_Championships_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_time_trial" title="2015 UCI Road World Championships \xe2\x80\x93 Men&#39;s time trial">2015 Road World Time Trial Championship</a>, and middle distance runner <a href="/wiki/Maryna_Arzamasava" class="mw-redirect" title="Maryna Arzamasava">Maryna Arzamasava</a>, who won the gold medal in the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_800_metres" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics \xe2\x80\x93 Women&#39;s 800 metres">800m at the 2015 World Championships in Athletics</a>.\n</p><p>Belarus is also known for its strong rhythmic gymnasts. Noticeable gymnasts include <a href="/wiki/Inna_Zhukova" title="Inna Zhukova">Inna Zhukova</a>, who earned silver at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Beijing_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Beijing Olympics">2008 Beijing Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liubov_Charkashyna" title="Liubov Charkashyna">Liubov Charkashyna</a>, who earned bronze at the 2012 London Olympics and <a href="/wiki/Melitina_Staniouta" title="Melitina Staniouta">Melitina Staniouta</a>, Bronze All-Around Medalist of the 2015 World Championships. The Belorussian senior group earned bronze at the <a href="/wiki/2012_London_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 London Olympics">2012 London Olympics</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Andrei_Arlovski" title="Andrei Arlovski">Andrei Arlovski</a>, who was born in <a href="/wiki/Babruysk" title="Babruysk">Babruysk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Byelorussian SSR</a>, is a current <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC</a> fighter and the former <a href="/wiki/List_of_UFC_champions" title="List of UFC champions">UFC heavyweight champion of the world</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Belarus" title="Telecommunications in Belarus">Telecommunications in Belarus</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_Belarus" title="Censorship in Belarus">Censorship in Belarus</a></div>\n<ul><li>Country code: <a href="/wiki/.by" title=".by">.by</a></li></ul>\n<p>The state telecom monopoly, Beltelecom, holds the exclusive interconnection with Internet providers outside of Belarus. Beltelecom owns all the backbone channels that linked to the Lattelecom, TEO LT, <a href="/wiki/Tata_Communications" title="Tata Communications">Tata Communications</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Teleglobe" class="mw-redirect" title="Teleglobe">Teleglobe</a>), Synterra, <a href="/wiki/Rostelecom" title="Rostelecom">Rostelecom</a>, Transtelekom and MTS ISP\'s. Beltelecom is the only operator licensed to provide commercial VoIP services in Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-ONI-Belarus-Nov2010_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONI-Belarus-Nov2010-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Heritage_Sites">World Heritage Sites</span></h3>\n<p>Belarus has four <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>-designated <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Mir_Castle_Complex" title="Mir Castle Complex">Mir Castle Complex</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nesvizh_Castle" title="Nesvizh Castle">Nesvizh Castle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Bia\xc5\x82owie\xc5\xbca Forest">Belovezhskaya Pushcha</a> (shared with <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Struve_Geodetic_Arc" title="Struve Geodetic Arc">Struve Geodetic Arc</a> (shared with nine other countries).<sup id="cite_ref-UNSECO_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSECO-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Flag_of_Belarus.svg/32px-Flag_of_Belarus.svg.png" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer thumbborder"
